## ðŸŽ¯ Quest 1.3: BLOOD MONEY

**Level:** 3  
**Duration:** 2-3 sessions  
**Objective:** Hunt down and eliminate a "bandit leader" terrorizing trade routes  
**Key NPCs:** Elara Thornwood, Merchant Consortium, Elara's Peasant Followers  
**Rewards:** 500gp (if completing contract), Variable based on choices  
**Location:** Thornwood Forest, 30 miles from Crossroads

### **Quest HOOK**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*Varak summons you to his office. On his desk sits a contract sealed with multiple wax sealsâ€”expensive paper, official-looking. When you enter, he's reading it with unusual interest.*
>
{{descriptive
*"High-value contract just came in. Merchant Consortiumâ€”legitimate business alliance from three cities. They're offering 500 gold to eliminate a bandit problem. That's exceptional pay for your level. Which means it's dangerous, complicated, or both."*
>
{{descriptive
*He slides the contract across.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Target is 'Red Wolf'â€”bandit leader operating in Thornwood Forest. Been hitting merchant caravans for six months. Dozen successful raids, zero survivors who fought back. The Consortium wants her dead. Publicly. As an example. They're offering an extra 100 gold if you bring back her head."*
>
{{descriptive
*He leans back.*
>
{{descriptive
*"I'm recommending you for this. You've proven competent. But this isn't entry-level work. Red Wolf has a gangâ€”estimates say 15-20 fighters. They know the forest. They're disciplined. This is your first real test. Interested?"*

### **The CONTRACT**

**Client:** Merchant Consortium (legitimate business alliance)  
**Target:** "Red Wolf" - bandit leader in Thornwood Forest  
**Payment:** 500gp for elimination, +100gp for bringing head  
**Deadline:** Two weeks  
**Terms:** "Target must be confirmed dead. Gang must be scattered or eliminated. Bring proof."

**If PCs investigate the contract (Investigation DC 12):**
- All legal language is proper
- Multiple merchant houses signed it
- Contract is legitimate, not a setup

**If PCs ask Varak questions:**

**"What do you know about Red Wolf?"**  
*"Not much. Uses that name as an alias. Femaleâ€”that's confirmed. Good tactician. Hits fast, retreats faster. Never leaves survivors. Professional operation, not desperate criminals."*

**"Why don't the merchants hire an army?"**  
*"Politics. Thornwood sits between Thaldros and Aethoria territoriesâ€”neither kingdom wants to send troops into disputed land. Creates diplomatic incidents. Cheaper to hire mercenaries. If you fail and die, no political fallout."*

**"What's our backup?"**  
*"None. You're it. The Consortium tried hiring local militiaâ€”they got ambushed, lost half their men, survivors refused to go back. You're attempt number three."*

**"Any intel on the gang?"**  
*"Here."* (Hands over report) *"Eyewitness accounts. Not much. Well-armed, well-trained, loyal to Red Wolf. That's unusual for banditsâ€”loyalty usually bought with fear or gold. This crew seems... different. Motivated."*

### **Investigation Phase**

Before hunting Red Wolf, smart PCs will investigate. Multiple sources available:

#### **Merchant Consortium Headquarters**

**Location:** Millford (1 day travel from Crossroads)

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*The Consortium headquarters is an impressive stone buildingâ€”guild hall meets fortress. Inside, clerks bustle about managing trade manifests. You're directed to the office of Guildmaster Henrik Voss.*
>
{{descriptive
*Voss is a portly man in expensive robes, fingers heavy with rings. He smiles when you enterâ€”the smile of someone used to buying solutions.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Ah! The mercenaries! Excellent! Have you killed that bandit bitch yet?"*

**NPC: Guildmaster Henrik Voss**

*Medium humanoid (human), lawful evil*

**Appearance:** 50s, overweight, expensive clothing, multiple rings, calculating eyes

**Personality:**
- Greedy, entitled, sees people as commodities
- Genuinely afraid of Red Wolf (she's cost him money)
- Believes wealth = righteousness
- Will lie about anything convenient

**Stats:** Use Noble (CR 1/8), won't fight

**If PCs ask questions:**

**"Tell us about Red Wolf:"**  
*"Criminal scum! She's been hitting our caravans for six months! Twelve successful raids! We've lost 10,000 gold in cargo! She steals everythingâ€”textiles, spices, tools, even food shipments meant for cities!"*

**"Why does she hit your routes specifically?"**  
*"Because we're successful! Thieves always target those who have something worth stealing! It's harassment, pure and simple!"*

**"What happened to the lands she operates in?"**  
*"Thornwood? Used to belong to some minor noble family. House Thornwood or something. They lost it years agoâ€”bad investments, debts, royal seizure. Sad story. Irrelevant. The land is Consortium property now. Legal and proper."*

**Investigation/Insight:**

**DC 13 Insight:** Voss is nervous about something beyond lost profits. He's worried about exposure.

**DC 15 Investigation (if searching office):** Find legal documents showing Consortium purchased "Thornwood Estate" from crown for remarkably low price (10,000gp for lands worth 100,000gp+). Dated 5 years ago.

**DC 18 Investigation (deeper search):** Find second set of documentsâ€”forged tax records showing House Thornwood "owed massive debts to crown." The debts were fabricated. This was a land grab using false legal documents.

**If PCs confront Voss with evidence:**

*"That's... that's all legal! Crown-approved! We followed proper procedures! If there were... irregularities... that's the crown's fault, not ours! We're victims here! That's why Red Wolf is targeting usâ€”she's a thief and criminal!"*

**The Truth (PCs won't know yet):** Consortium bribed corrupt officials to create fake debts, seized Thornwood lands, evicted the noble family. Everything legal on paper, completely fraudulent in reality.

#### **Thornwood Village**

**Location:** Small village near the forest (half-day from Millford)

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*Thornwood village is... wrong. At first glance, it's a typical hamletâ€”thatched cottages, small farms, a well in the square. But something's off. The people are too quiet. When you pass, they watch with guarded expressions. Suspicious. Afraid. Not of youâ€”of something else.*
>
{{descriptive
*An elderly woman sweeps her doorstep. When you approach, she stops. Looks at your weapons. Then meets your eyes with defiance born of fear.*
>
{{descriptive
*"You here to hunt the Wolf?"*

**NPC: Grandmother Petra**

*Medium humanoid (human), neutral good*

**Appearance:** 70s, weathered face, peasant clothing, steel in her eyes

**Personality:**
- Protective of village
- Knows the truth
- Won't volunteer information (protects Red Wolf)
- Will talk if persuaded or if PCs show they're not blindly following contract

**If PCs are openly carrying contract or mention merchants:**

*"Then you can leave. We don't help murderers."*

**If PCs try Persuasion or Insight:**

**DC 14 Persuasion:** *"We're not here to kill innocents. We want the truth. What's really happening?"*

**Success:**

{{descriptive
*She eyes you for a long moment. Then sighs.*
>
{{descriptive
*"The Wolf isn't a bandit. She's Lady Elara Thornwood. This was her family's land. The merchantsâ€”those vulturesâ€”they stole it. Bribed the crown, faked documents, evicted her family. Her father died of grief. Her mother followed a year later."*
>
{{descriptive
*"Elara didn't become a bandit. She became a rebel. Every caravan she hits? That's cargo bought with stolen wealth. Every 'stolen' shipment? Half goes to the poor, half funds her attempt to reclaim what's hers. She's not terrorizing tradeâ€”she's reclaiming stolen property."*
>
{{descriptive
*"You kill her, you kill the only person fighting for justice. You help the merchants, you help thieves. Choose wisely, sellsword."*

**If PCs ask about the villagers:**

*"We follow her. By choice. When the Consortium took the lands, they raised our rents, seized our harvests, treated us like slaves. Elara could have fled, started over somewhere else. She stayed. She fights for us. So we fight for her."*

**If PCs ask where to find Red Wolf:**

*"I won't tell you. But... if you go into Thornwood Forest, she'll find you. She knows everything that happens in these woods. If you're not here to murder her, say so. Loudly. Maybe she'll talk instead of shooting."*

### **The Forest - Entering Red Wolf'S Territory**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*Thornwood Forest is ancientâ€”massive oaks and pines that block out the sun. The merchant road cuts through it, wide enough for wagons but bordered by dense undergrowth. Perfect ambush terrain.*
>
{{descriptive
*You've been walking for an hour when you notice: too quiet. No birds. No small animals. You're being watched.*
>
{{descriptive
*Then you see them. Figures step from the treesâ€”ten, fifteen, twenty armed men and women, bows drawn, arrows nocked. Not bandits. Too organized. They wear mismatched armor but carry themselves like soldiers.*
>
{{descriptive
*A woman steps forward. Mid-twenties, auburn hair tied back, leather armor worn but well-maintained. A longsword at her hip. Her eyes are hard, calculating. A leader.*
>
{{descriptive
*"You're the mercenaries the Consortium hired. I'd ask how I know, but my people saw you leaving Millford. Now here's your choice: turn around and leave, or die here. I'm giving you one chance because I'm not a murderer. But I will defend my land and my people."*

**NPC: Elara Thornwood / "RED WOLF"**

*Medium humanoid (human), chaotic good*

**Appearance:** 26 years old, auburn hair, green eyes, lean and scarred from forest living, carries herself like nobility despite rough clothing

**Personality:**
- Driven by justice (from her perspective)
- Willing to kill in defense, but not eager
- Protective of her followers (they're her people)
- Bitter about the system that destroyed her family
- Practicalâ€”knows she can't beat an army, so uses guerrilla tactics

**Stats:** Use **Bandit Captain** (CR 2) but with modifications:
- HP: 65 (10d8 + 20)
- AC: 16 (studded leather +1)
- Skills: Add History +4, Insight +5, Persuasion +5
- Equipment: Longsword +1, Longbow, studded leather +1

**Her Followers:** 20 **Bandits** (CR 1/8) and 5 **Veterans** (CR 3)
- Mix of former soldiers and loyal peasants
- Well-trained (Elara trained them)
- Loyal to the death (they believe in her cause)

### **The CONFRONTATION**

This scene can go multiple ways depending on PC approach:

#### **Approach 1: Immediate Combat**

If PCs attack without talking:

**Combat Encounter:**
- 1 Elara Thornwood (CR 2, enhanced)
- 5 Veterans (CR 3 each)
- 20 Bandits (CR 1/8 each)

**Total CR:** ~12 encounter (DEADLY for level 3 party)

**Tactics:**
- Elara calls for focused fire on spellcasters
- Veterans protect Elara
- Bandits use hit-and-run tactics
- If Elara drops below 20 HP, she calls retreat
- Forest terrain gives them advantage (they know every tree)
- They'll use guerrilla tacticsâ€”fall back, ambush, repeat

**If PCs Win:**
- Collect Elara's head (if they want the bonus 100gp)
- Loot bodies (200gp in mixed gear and coins)
- Return to Consortium, collect 500-600gp
- **Consequence:** Villagers hate you, you've killed rightful heir, Consortium thrilled
- **Reputation:** Ruthless, follows contracts above all

**If PCs Lose:**
- Elara captures survivors (she won't kill unconscious enemies)
- Takes their weapons, releases them at forest edge
- Warning: "Go back to Crossroads. Tell the Consortium the Wolf won't be hunted. Tell them to return what they stole or I'll burn every caravan they send."
- **Consequence:** Failed contract, reputation hit, lose deposit

#### **Approach 2: Negotiation**

If PCs try to talk:

**Persuasion DC 14:** "We want to hear your side before we make a decision."

**Success:**

{{descriptive
*Elara eyes you warily, then nods.*
>
{{descriptive
*"You want the truth? Fine. Here it is: Five years ago, my family owned this land. House Thornwoodâ€”minor nobility, but we were fair lords. We cared for our people."*
>
{{descriptive
*"Then the merchants came. Henrik Voss and his Consortium. They wanted our landâ€”it's on a prime trade route. We refused to sell. So they fabricated debts. Bribed crown officials. Forged tax records. Made it look like we owed the kingdom 50,000 gold."*
>
{{descriptive
*"The crown seized our lands. 'Sold' them to the Consortium for a fraction of their value. My father tried to fight it legally. He died of a broken heart before the trial finished. My mother followed six months later."*
>
{{descriptive
*"I had nothing. My birthright stolen by legal theft. So I took it backâ€”one caravan at a time. Every piece of cargo I 'steal' is property bought with wealth stolen from my family. I'm not a bandit. I'm reclaiming what's mine."*
>
{{descriptive
*She looks at you directly.*
>
{{descriptive
*"So here's your choice, mercenaries: Kill me and help thieves keep stolen land. Or help me get justice. Or walk away and let us settle this ourselves. But know what you're choosing."*

**If PCs ask for proof:**

*"I have the original land deeds. The real tax recordsâ€”the ones before they were forged. Letters from my father to lawyers, showing the fabricated debts. All hidden in case I need them for a legal challenge."*

She can provide this evidence (Investigation DC 10 confirms it's legitimate).

### **The CHOICE**

**Option 1: Complete the Contract (Kill Elara)**
- Fight begins (as per Combat approach above)
- Collect 500-600gp from Consortium
- **Consequence:** 
  - Killed legitimate heir
  - Helped corrupt merchants
  - Villagers become enemies
  - Earned reputation as mercenary who follows contracts regardless of morality
  - Varak approves (contract honored)
- **Alignment:** Lawful Neutral or Evil (depending on motivation)

**Option 2: Switch Sides (Help Elara)**
- Break contract with Consortium
- Help Elara reclaim her lands legally or by force
- **Sub-options:**
  - Legal: Take evidence to authorities (DC 18 Persuasion, weeks of effort)
  - Force: Help her raid Consortium headquarters
  - Compromise: Negotiate settlement between parties
- **Consequence:**
  - Lose contract payment (500gp)
  - Gain Elara's friendship (+1 noble ally for Act II)
  - Consortium becomes enemy
  - Reputation hit with merchants
  - Varak is FURIOUS (broke contract)â€”you're expelled from guild unless you have very good explanation
- **Alignment:** Chaotic Good, "right over rules"

**Option 3: Broker a Deal**
- Persuasion DC 18: Convince both parties to settle
- Elara wants: Her title restored OR 50,000gp compensation OR Consortium exiled
- Consortium wants: Elara stops raids OR Elara leaves region OR Elara dead
- Finding middle ground: VERY DIFFICULT
- Possible compromise: Consortium pays Elara 25,000gp to go away, keeps land, Elara rebuilds elsewhere
- **Consequence:**
  - Both sides moderately satisfied
  - You get paid by both (250gp from each = 500gp total)
  - Reputation as mediator
  - Neither side loves you, but both respect you
- **Alignment:** True Neutral, pragmatic problem-solver

**Option 4: Play Both Sides**
- Fake Elara's death (Deception DC 16)
- Bring "proof" to Consortium (need convincing fake evidence)
- Elara goes into hiding, waits for heat to cool
- Collect 600gp from Consortium
- Elara pays you 200gp from her stolen wealth
- **Consequence:**
  - 800gp total profit
  - Very riskyâ€”if discovered, both sides want you dead
  - Reputation as clever but untrustworthy
  - Elara becomes hidden ally (might return in Act II)
- **Alignment:** Chaotic Neutral, opportunistic

**Option 5: Expose the Consortium Publicly**
- Take evidence to authorities (if operating in Thaldros territory)
- Public trial ensues (DC 16 Persuasion to get officials to care)
- Success: Consortium investigated, lands might be returned
- Failure: Officials are also corrupt, bury evidence
- **Consequence:**
  - No payment from Consortium (they're arrested or fleeing)
  - Elara rewards you with her remaining family treasures (worth 400gp)
  - Major reputation boost with common folk
  - Enemies in merchant and noble circles
  - Complicated with guild (broke contract for "moral reasons")
- **Alignment:** Lawful Good, systemic justice

**Option 6: Walk Away**
- Refuse to take either side
- Return contract to Varak uncompleted
- Tell both parties to handle it themselves
- **Consequence:**
  - No payment
  - No enemies made
  - Reputation as neutral/cowardly (depending on who's judging)
  - Varak is disappointed but understands (unusual situation)
  - Option to return later in campaign if situation unresolved
- **Alignment:** True Neutral, non-intervention

### **Special Option: Creative Solutions**

If PCs come up with creative solution not listed:

**Examples:**
- Hire Elara as consultant to hunt "herself" (she gets paid, Consortium thinks she's dead)
- Frame someone else as Red Wolf
- Help Elara raid merchant HQ for documents proving fraud
- Marry Elara to a PC (noble title restored through marriage?)
- etc.

**DM should reward creativity** with partial success and unique consequences.

### **Returning to VARAK**

Varak's response varies dramatically based on choice:

#### **If You Completed Contract:**

{{descriptive
*Varak counts out 500 gold.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Consortium confirmed the kill. Contract fulfilled. Good work."*
>
{{descriptive
*He pauses.*
>
{{descriptive
*"I'm hearing rumors about what you learned out there. About the land grab. The forged documents. The dispossessed noble. I assume you know the truth?"*
>
{{descriptive
*(If PCs confirm)*
>
{{descriptive
*"And you killed her anyway. Interesting. That's the business we're inâ€”we don't judge the morality of contracts, just complete them. Some mercenaries can't handle that. You can. That's valuable. Ruthless, but valuable."*
>
{{descriptive
*(He slides a small iron ring acrossâ€”a veteran guild member token)*
>
{{descriptive
*"You're moving up. But remember: reputation is everything. You're now known as someone who follows contracts no matter what. That opens doors with some clients. Closes them with others. Live with it."*

#### **If You Switched Sides:**

{{descriptive
*Varak's face is stone.*
>
{{descriptive
*"You broke a contract. You sided with the target against the client. That's grounds for expulsionâ€”or execution, depending on how angry I am."*
>
{{descriptive
*(He leans forward)*
>
{{descriptive
*"But I've read the evidence Elara provided. The Consortium's land grab was fraud. Legally permitted fraud, but fraud nonetheless. You chose justice over contract. Idiotic, but I understand the impulse."*
>
{{descriptive
*(He sighs)*
>
{{descriptive
*"Here's your punishment: 30 days suspension from guild. No contracts, no guild services, no protection. You're on your own for a month. After that, you're back inâ€”but your reputation is damaged. Half the merchants won't work with you. The other half will pay extra for your 'integrity.'"*
>
{{descriptive
*(He stands)*
>
{{descriptive
*"Learn this lesson: in this business, breaking a contract should cost you more than keeping it. You got off light because the client was fraudulent. Next time, you won't be so lucky."*

#### **If You Brokered A Deal:**

{{descriptive
*Varak actually smilesâ€”rare.*
>
{{descriptive
*"You turned a blood feud into a settlement. Both parties walked away moderately satisfied. No one died. Everyone got something."*
>
{{descriptive
*(Counts out gold from both payments)*
>
{{descriptive
*"That's rare in this business. Most mercenaries are hammersâ€”every problem is a nail. You used your head instead of your sword. That's the kind of thinking that makes you more than just muscle."*
>
{{descriptive
*(Slides contract across)*
>
{{descriptive
*"Private contract. One of my personal clients. They need a... delicate situation handled. Not combat. Negotiation. Blackmail. Subtle work. Pays triple normal rates. Interested? You've earned it."*

**This opens path to higher-tier contracts in Act II.**

#### **If You Played Both Sides:**

{{descriptive
*Varak eyes you carefully.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Consortium believes Red Wolf is dead. Red Wolf has vanished from the region. Both parties satisfied. Contract technically fulfilled."*
>
{{descriptive
*(Long pause)*
>
{{descriptive
*"I don't know what you actually did out there. I don't want to know. But I'm hearing whispers that Red Wolf might not be as dead as the Consortium thinks. If that's true, and they find out, they'll come after you. So will everyone you lied to."*
>
{{descriptive
*(He slides the payment across)*
>
{{descriptive
*"You're clever. Clever people either get rich or get dead. Usually both, in that order. Watch your back."*

### **Consequences For Act Ii**

Track the following based on choice:

**Allies Gained:**
- Elara Thornwood (if helped her) - noble ally, potential romance option
- Merchant Consortium (if killed Elara) - economic ally
- Village of Thornwood (if helped Elara) - common folk support

**Enemies Made:**
- Merchant Consortium (if betrayed them) - wealthy enemies
- Elara's followers (if killed her) - guerrilla fighters hunting you
- Other mercenaries (if broke contract) - reputation damage

**Reputation Shifts:**
- "Ruthless Contractor" (if killed Elara despite truth)
- "Idealistic Fool" (if helped Elara)
- "Clever Mediator" (if brokered deal)
- "Untrustworthy Trickster" (if played both sides)

**Guild Status:**
- Full member (if completed contract or brokered deal)
- Suspended (if broke contract)
- Expelled (if broke contract violently)

---

## Quest 1.3 - DM Guidance

### **Design Philosophy**

This quest is about **moral complexity in systems**:

**The Dilemma:**
- Elara is legitimately wronged (fraud victim)
- But she's also committed crimes (robbery, assault)
- Consortium legally owns the land (corrupt process, but legal)
- But their ownership is based on fraud
- **Who's right? Who's wrong? Both? Neither?**

**The Test:**
- Will PCs follow contracts blindly?
- Will they break contracts for "righteousness"?
- Can they find middle ground?
- Are they mercenaries or heroes?

### **Key DMing Points**

**1. Present Both Sides Fairly**

Don't make Consortium cartoonishly evil or Elara saintly:
- Consortium genuinely believes business is business
- Elara has killed people (guards who fought back)
- Both have blood on their hands
- Both have valid arguments

**2. Respect All Choices**

Every option in this quest is valid:
- Killing Elara for profit? Valid (mercenary thinking)
- Helping Elara? Valid (justice thinking)
- Staying neutral? Valid (self-preservation)
- Getting creative? Valid (problem-solving)

**3. Consequences Matter**

Whatever PCs choose has lasting effects:
- Break contract? Guild suspends you
- Kill Elara? Villagers remember
- Help Elara? Merchants remember
- Play both sides? Everyone remembers

**4. No Correct Answer**

This quest has no "right" choice, only consequences:
- Players should debate this
- Characters should have different opinions
- Party might split on decision
- That's the point

### **Difficulty Adjustments**

**If Party Struggling:**
- Reduce Elara's follower count (15 instead of 25)
- Give more obvious clues about the fraud
- Make Consortium more obviously evil
- Offer easier Persuasion DCs

**If Party Dominating:**
- Add more followers to Elara's force
- Make Consortium more sympathetic (they didn't know about fraud)
- Add time pressure (Consortium sends second mercenary team)
- Make consequences more severe

### **Roleplaying Elara**

Elara should be **complex, not simple**:

**She's not a victim:**
- She chose this path
- She's killed people
- She's a rebel, not a martyr

**She's not a villain:**
- She's fighting for justice
- She protects her people
- She's willing to talk before fighting

**She's human:**
- Tired of running
- Wants her home back
- Knows she might lose
- Appreciates honesty

**Key Dialogue Beats:**

*"I'm not asking you to be heroes. I'm asking you to not be murderers."*

*"You think I wanted this? I had a castle. A title. A future. The Consortium took that. So I took it back, one caravan at a time."*

*"Kill me if you want. But know what you're doingâ€”you're helping rich men stay rich by killing the people they stole from."*

### **Common Player Questions**

**"Is there a legal solution?"**
Yes, but very difficult (DC 18+ checks, weeks of time, corrupt officials)

**"Can we blackmail the Consortium with evidence?"**
Absolutely! Creative solution rewarded.

**"What if we just take the evidence and sell it to highest bidder?"**
Chaotic Neutral optionâ€”both sides might pay to suppress it.

**"Can we take over the territory ourselves?"**
Technically yes, but requires army/resources PCs don't have at level 3.

### **This Quest Tests:**

- **Contract vs. Conscience** - What wins?
- **Profit vs. Principles** - Which matters more?
- **System vs. Justice** - Can legal be wrong?
- **Pragmatism vs. Idealism** - Where's the line?

---

**Quest 1.3 Complete - ~5,500 Words**

**Total Act I Content So Far: ~16,800 Words**

**NPCs to Add:**
- Elara Thornwood / Red Wolf (Bandit Captain, enhanced)
- Guildmaster Henrik Voss (Noble, coward)
- Grandmother Petra (Commoner)
- Elara's Veterans (5x Veteran)
- Elara's Followers (20x Bandit)

**Items:**
- Elara's Family Evidence (plot item)
- Elara's Longsword +1 (if killed)
- Thornwood Signet Ring (if allied)

**Next Up: Quest 1.4 - The Neutral Ground (Guild Power Struggle)**

# Quest 2.1: The Recruiters

## Blood & Coin Campaign - Act II Opening

**Level:** 6  
**Duration:** 2-3 sessions  
**Objective:** Meet three faction recruiters, investigate them, choose allegiance  
**Key NPCs:** Commander Dawnblade, Envoy Valen, Corvus Blackwood  
**Rewards:** 1,000-2,500gp upfront + faction access  
**Theme:** "The Interview"

---

## Quest Setup

**Time:** Six months after Quest 1.5 (Act I finale)

**What's Changed:**
- Your reputation has spread across both kingdoms
- Regional tensions escalating toward war
- Naval skirmishes increasing
- Trade routes disrupted
- Everyone choosing sides

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*Six months have passed since [reference their Act I ending]. Life in Crossroads continuedâ€”contracts, gold, survival. But the world beyond hasn't been idle.*
>
{{descriptive
*Rumors of war spread like wildfire. The Crown and the frontier territoriesâ€”in tension for decadesâ€”are now at each other's throats. Trade conflicts. Assassinations. Embargo threats. Everyone sees it coming.*
>
{{descriptive
*And everyone wants mercenaries.*
>
{{descriptive
*This morning, three separate messages arrived for you. Three different factions. Three offers. All arriving the same day.*
>
{{descriptive
*That can't be coincidence.*

---

## The Three Messages

**PCs receive three sealed letters:**

### **Message 1: Royal Seal**

*Ornate envelope, wax seal bearing crown of Thaldros*

{{descriptive
**"To the Mercenaries of [their group name/reputation]:**
>
> Your services are requested by Commander Helena Dawnblade of the Royal Army of Thaldros. A matter of national importance and significant compensation.
>
> Present yourselves at the Wayward Inn, private room, today at noon.
>
> Discretion is expected. Professionalism will be rewarded.
>
{{descriptive
**â€”Commander H. Dawnblade, Knight-Commander, Order of the Dawn"**

---

*Simple paper, no seal, republican symbol stamped*

>
> The Aetheran Council needs capable individuals who understand that freedom is worth fighting for. Envoy Marcus Valen wishes to discuss an opportunity that serves both your interests and the cause of their alliance.
>
> Wayward Inn, private room, today at 2pm.
>
> Come if you believe people deserve to choose their own destiny.
>

*No seal, no signature, just an address and time*

> Those with vision are needed. Those with courage are welcome.
>
> Wayward Inn, private room, today at 4pm.
>

>
{{descriptive
**â€”A Friend"**

## The Wayward Inn

### **Location**

A well-known neutral ground in Crossroads. No guild affiliations. No political loyalties. Perfect for clandestine meetings.

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*The Wayward Inn sits on the border between Iron Guild and Black Chains territoryâ€”neutral ground by necessity. It's where deals get made when both sides need to pretend they're not cooperating.*
>
{{descriptive
*The innkeeper, Old Marcus, is famous for two things: excellent whiskey and aggressive neutrality. He'll throw out anyone who starts trouble, regardless of guild, rank, or gold.*
>
{{descriptive
*Three private rooms have been reserved today. All paid in advance. All requesting the same mercenaries.*
>
{{descriptive
*Someone's been coordinating.*

---

## Meeting 1: Commander Helena Dawnblade (Noon)

### **The Setting**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*The first private room is tastefully appointed. A fire crackles. Wine and cheese set out. Military precision in every detail.*
>
{{descriptive
*Commander Helena Dawnblade stands by the window, backlit by noon sun. She's imposingâ€”six feet tall, silver armor polished to mirror sheen, holy symbol of Thaldros prominent on her chest. Late 40s, steel-grey hair in tight braid, face bearing scars from decades of service.*
>
{{descriptive
*She turns as you enter. Her eyes assess you with military efficiency.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Sit," she says. Not a request. "We have much to discuss and little time for pleasantries."*

---

## Npc: Commander Helena Dawnblade

*Medium humanoid (human), lawful neutral*

**Armor Class:** 18 (plate armor)  
**Hit Points:** 143 (22d8 + 44)  
**Speed:** 30 ft.

**STR** 18 (+4) | **DEX** 12 (+1) | **CON** 14 (+2)  
**INT** 14 (+2) | **WIS** 16 (+3) | **CHA** 17 (+3)

**Saving Throws:** Wis +7, Cha +7  
**Skills:** Athletics +8, Insight +7, Intimidation +7, Persuasion +7, Religion +6  
**Senses:** Passive Perception 13  
**Languages:** Common, Celestial, Dwarvish  
**Challenge:** 10 (5,900 XP)

**Divine Sense (3/Day).** Can detect celestials, fiends, and undead within 60 feet.

**Lay on Hands (50 HP/Day).** Can heal as an action.

**Aura of Protection.** Allies within 10 feet gain +3 to saving throws.

**Improved Divine Smite.** Melee attacks deal extra 1d8 radiant damage.

#### Actions

**Multiattack.** Three longsword attacks.

**Longsword +2.** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target.  
*Hit:* 11 (1d8 + 7) slashing damage, or 12 (1d10 + 7) if used with two hands, plus 4 (1d8) radiant damage.

**Divine Smite (Spell Slot).** When she hits with melee attack, can expend spell slot to deal extra 2d8 (1st level) to 5d8 (4th level) radiant damage.

#### Spellcasting

**Spellcasting Ability:** Charisma (spell save DC 15, +7 to hit)

**Spells Prepared:**
- 1st level (4 slots): *bless, cure wounds, divine favor, shield of faith*
- 2nd level (3 slots): *aid, lesser restoration, zone of truth*
- 3rd level (3 slots): *crusader's mantle, dispel magic, revivify*
- 4th level (1 slot): *banishment, death ward*

#### Personality & Motivation

**Age:** 48  
**Appearance:** Imposing, armored, grey hair, battle-scarred, stern but not cruel

**Personality:**
- Career soldier who believes in order
- Lawful neutral (not goodâ€”follows orders)
- Uncomfortable with politics but loyal to crown
- Respects competence, despises incompetence
- Knows Thaldros is flawed but believes it's better than chaos
- Will do terrible things for "greater good"

**Background:**
- 30 years of service to Thaldros
- Rose through ranks via merit
- Earned paladin oath through devotion to order
- Has done questionable things for crown
- Believes strong government prevents anarchy
- Sees war as necessary to preserve civilization

**Motivation:**
- Genuinely believes Thaldros must win
- Fears Aethoria's democracy will spread chaos
- Willing to hire morally flexible mercenaries
- Respects PCs' proven capabilities
- Needs operatives who "get things done"

---

### **Dawnblade'S Pitch**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*She pours wineâ€”expensive vintageâ€”and slides a glass toward you.*
>
{{descriptive
*"I'll be direct. War is coming. Aethoria's 'democracy' threatens regional stability. Mob rule dressed as freedom. If they win, chaos spreads. Trade collapses. Bandits rule. Society crumbles.*
>
{{descriptive
*Thaldros is order. Civilization. Law. We've maintained peace for 500 years through strength and structure. We intend to continue.*
>
{{descriptive
*I'm assembling a team of... specialists. Professionals who understand that sometimes order requires difficult choices. Your reputation suggests you're such professionals.*
>
{{descriptive
*Work for the crown. Significant compensation. Legal protection. Political connections. And when we winâ€”not if, WHENâ€”you'll be on the winning side."*

**She slides a contract across the table:**

**The Offer:**
- **Upfront Payment:** 2,500 gold pieces (deposited today)
- **Per Mission:** 1,000-2,000gp depending on difficulty
- **Authority:** Deputized as crown agents (can act with royal authority)
- **Protection:** Legal immunity for actions taken under orders
- **Post-War Rewards:** Lands, titles, or additional gold (10,000gp minimum)

**The Expectations:**
- Intelligence gathering on Aethoria military
- Sabotage of enemy supply lines
- "Neutralization" of key targets (assassination)
- Publicly: "Defending the kingdom"
- Privately: "Whatever's necessary to win"

---

### **Questions & Answers**

**If PCs ask questions:**

**"Why us specifically?"**
{{descriptive
*"Your work speaks for itself. [Reference Act I achievements]. You're competent. More importantly, you understand grey areas. Perfect soldiers follow orders without question. Perfect mercenaries complete contracts despite complications. I need the latter."*

**"What if we refuse?"**
{{descriptive
*"Then you refuse. I'm not the Aethoria mobâ€”I don't force allegiance. But this war will touch everyone. Neutrality becomes harder every day. Choose a side, or have one chosen for you."*

**"Is Thaldros really the 'good guys'?"**
{{descriptive
*(If PCs reference Quest 1.5 and Marcus Blackwood's trial)*
{{descriptive
*"Good? No. Better? Yes. Thaldros has problemsâ€”I won't deny it. Corruption exists. Justice isn't always just. But compare us to Aethoria's chaos. We're stable. Functional. That matters."*

**"What about civilian casualties?"**
{{descriptive
*"War has costs. I'll give you missions with... clear objectives. How you achieve them is your discretion. I need results, not reports on methods. Does that answer your question?"*

**Insight DC 15:**
- Dawnblade is sincere but knows she's hiring for morally grey work
- She's uncomfortable with some orders from above
- Respects PCs enough to be honest about what's expected
- Will follow orders even if they're war crimes

**Persuasion DC 18 (to get her to reveal doubts):**
{{descriptive
*(Privately, checking no one listening)*
{{descriptive
*"Off the record? I've served Thaldros 30 years. I've seen it do great things and terrible things. But I've also seen what happens when government collapses. Famine. Warlords. Suffering.*
>
{{descriptive
*Order is worth defending, even when order is imperfect. That's my oath. If you can't accept that, walk away now. No judgment."*

---

### **Dawnblade'S Secret Agenda**

**What she's NOT telling PCs:**

1. **Scapegoat Plan:** Crown intends to frame mercenaries for war crimes post-war
2. **Marcus Blackwood:** If PCs helped him (Quest 1.5), crown remembersâ€”sees them as potential troublemakers
3. **Her Doubts:** She suspects some missions will be atrocities but will follow orders anyway
4. **The War:** High command knows war is partly manufactured for political reasons

**This information revealed later in Quest 2.3 (The Double Cross)**

---

## Meeting 2: Envoy Marcus Valen (2pm)

### **The Setting**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*Same inn, different room. This one is simplerâ€”wooden table, local wine, no extravagance. A statement.*
>
{{descriptive
*Envoy Marcus Valen stands as you enter. He's in his 50s, wearing republican robes (no finery), grey beard, warm eyes, genuine smile. He looks tired but hopeful.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Welcome, friends." His voice is warm, practiced. "Thank you for coming. Please, sit. I know Commander Dawnblade made her pitch this morning. Now hear ours."*

---

## Npc: Envoy Marcus Valen

*Medium humanoid (human), chaotic good*

**Armor Class:** 12 (15 with *mage armor*)  
**Hit Points:** 78 (12d8 + 24)  
**Speed:** 30 ft.

**STR** 10 (+0) | **DEX** 14 (+2) | **CON** 14 (+2)  
**INT** 16 (+3) | **WIS** 15 (+2) | **CHA** 18 (+4)

**Saving Throws:** Int +6, Wis +5, Cha +7  
**Skills:** Deception +7, History +6, Insight +5, Persuasion +10  
**Senses:** Passive Perception 12  
**Languages:** Common, Elvish, Dwarvish, Sylvan  
**Challenge:** 6 (2,300 XP)

**Inspiring Leader.** Can spend 10 minutes inspiring up to 6 creatures, granting them temporary HP equal to level + Charisma modifier.

**Silver Tongue.** Advantage on Persuasion checks when arguing for democratic ideals.

**Political Network.** Has contacts throughout Aethoria and can call in favors.

#### Actions

**Dagger.** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 20/60 ft.  
*Hit:* 4 (1d4 + 2) piercing damage.

**Inspiring Speech (Recharge 5-6).** As an action, can grant allies within 30 feet advantage on their next attack roll or saving throw.

#### Spellcasting

**Spellcasting Ability:** Charisma (spell save DC 15, +7 to hit)

**Cantrips:** *friends, mage hand, minor illusion, prestidigitation*

**Spells Known:**
- 1st level (4 slots): *charm person, disguise self, mage armor, sleep*
- 2nd level (3 slots): *detect thoughts, suggestion, zone of truth*
- 3rd level (3 slots): *counterspell, sending, tongues*
- 4th level (2 slots): *compulsion, greater invisibility*

#### Personality & Motivation

**Age:** 54  
**Appearance:** Republican robes (simple), grey beard, warm eyes, tired but determined, genuine smile

**Personality:**
- True believer in democracy
- Charismatic and inspiring
- Idealistic but not naive (knows corruption exists)
- Genuinely cares about common people
- Willing to compromise principles to win
- "The ends justify the means" (sometimes)

**Background:**
- Former merchant who entered politics
- Rose through senate via popular support
- Lost family to Thaldros royal decree (land seizure)
- Believes democracy is humanity's future
- Understands Aethoria is flawed but fixable
- Willing to hire morally grey mercenaries

**Motivation:**
- Save democracy from monarchy
- Prove people can govern themselves
- Prevent Thaldros expansion
- Win war for republic's survival
- Knows Aethoria will make mistakes but believes in the system

---

### **Valen'S Pitch**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*He doesn't pour wine. He opens a bottle of local beerâ€”cheap, common, statement of solidarity.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Commander Dawnblade offered you gold and glory serving a king. I offer you a chance to serve something greater: freedom.*
>
{{descriptive
*Thaldros is a relic. Monarchy is a failed system where one family decides the fate of millions. The Aetheran Council is humanity's futureâ€”government by the people, for the people.*
>
{{descriptive
*Yes, we're messy. Democracy is loud, chaotic, inefficient. But it's OURS. We choose our leaders. We write our laws. We own our destiny.*
>
{{descriptive
*I won't lieâ€”we're outmatched militarily. Thaldros has more soldiers, more gold, more resources. But we have something they don't: we're fighting for something we believe in.*
>
{{descriptive
*Help us. Not for goldâ€”though we'll pay what we can. Not for powerâ€”though you'll be heroes of the revolution. Do it because tyranny must be opposed. Because people deserve to be free."*

**The contract he offers is handwritten, simple:**

**The Offer:**
- **Upfront Payment:** 1,500 gold pieces (less than Thaldros)
- **Per Mission:** 800-1,500gp depending on success
- **Authority:** Republican commission (less legal weight than crown)
- **Protection:** Popular support (common folk shelter you)
- **Post-War Rewards:** Citizenship, gratitude, historical recognition (not gold or lands)

**The Expectations:**
- Intelligence gathering on Thaldros nobility
- Smuggling weapons to resistance cells
- Protecting democratic leaders from assassination
- Publicly: "Fighting for freedom"
- Privately: "Winning at any cost"

---

### **Questions & Answers**

**If PCs ask questions:**

**"Why should we believe democracy works?"**
{{descriptive
*"Because it's already working. Look at Aethoriaâ€”we have problems, but we solve them through debate, not decree. When our leaders fail, we replace them. When Thaldros's king fails, people suffer for generations. Which system sounds better to you?"*

**"You're paying less than Thaldros."**
{{descriptive
*"We're a republic, not a monarchy. We don't have royal vaults. But what we offer is worth more than gold: you'll be on the right side of history. Your children will sing songs of how you fought tyranny. Can Dawnblade offer you that?"*

**"What if democracy fails?"**
{{descriptive
*"Then we'll have tried something noble and failed nobly. But I don't believe we'll fail. The people WANT freedom. They WANT choice. Thaldros rules through fear and tradition. We inspire through hope. Hope is stronger."*

**"Will you ask us to do terrible things?"**
{{descriptive
*(Pauses, uncomfortable)*
{{descriptive
*"War is terrible. Revolution is messy. Will I ask you to kill Thaldros soldiers? Yes. Sabotage supply lines? Yes. These are necessary evils to defeat a greater evil. I won't lie and say our hands stay clean. But we fight for a just cause. That matters."*

**Insight DC 14:**
- Valen is genuine but naive about some realities
- He believes in his cause deeply
- He knows Aethoria leadership has corruption too
- He's willing to compromise principles to win
- He sees PCs as tools for necessary evil

**Persuasion DC 16 (to get him to reveal doubts):**
{{descriptive
*"You want the truth? Aethoria isn't perfect. Some senators are corrupt. Some officials abuse power. Democracy doesn't eliminate human nature.*
>
{{descriptive
*But here's the difference: in Thaldros, when the king is corrupt, you're stuck with him for life. In Aethoria, we can vote him out. The system has safeguards. It's not perfect, but it's better. That's all I can promiseâ€”better, not perfect."*

---

### **Valen'S Secret Agenda**

**What he's NOT telling PCs:**

1. **Corruption:** Aethoria senate is more corrupt than he admits
2. **Post-War:** Some leaders plan to establish "temporary dictatorship" after victory
3. **Defector:** They're protecting a war criminal (General Thorne) for his intelligence
4. **The War:** Republic knows it's outmatched but hoping for guerrilla victory

**This information revealed later in Quest 2.3 (The Double Cross)**

---

## Meeting 3: Corvus Blackwood (4pm)

### **The Setting**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*The third room is different. No fire. Candles instead. Bookshelves lining walls. Maps of ancient ruins scattered on table. Occult symbolsâ€”not evil, just... old.*
>
{{descriptive
*A man stands with his back to you, studying a map. He's in his 50s, wearing scholar's robes, grey hair tied back. When he turns, his eyes are intenseâ€”not mad, but focused with frightening clarity.*
>
{{descriptive
*"You came." His voice is measured, educated. "Good. That means you're thinking. Dawnblade offered order through oppression. Valen offered chaos through democracy. I offer a third option: burn it all down and build something better."*
>
{{descriptive
*He gestures to chairs.*
>
{{descriptive
*"My name is Corvus Blackwood. And I'm going to save the world."*

---

## Npc: Corvus Blackwood

*Medium humanoid (human), chaotic neutral*

**Armor Class:** 15 (18 with *mage armor*)  
**Hit Points:** 99 (18d8 + 18)  
**Speed:** 30 ft.

**STR** 10 (+0) | **DEX** 16 (+3) | **CON** 12 (+1)  
**INT** 20 (+5) | **WIS** 14 (+2) | **CHA** 16 (+3)

**Saving Throws:** Int +10, Wis +7  
**Skills:** Arcana +15, History +15, Insight +7, Investigation +10, Persuasion +8, Religion +10  
**Damage Resistances:** psychic  
**Senses:** Passive Perception 12  
**Languages:** Common, Draconic, Elvish, Abyssal, Celestial, Primordial  
**Challenge:** 9 (5,000 XP)

**Arcane Recovery (1/Day).** Can recover spell slots during short rest (up to 9 levels total).

**Portent (3/Day).** Roll 3d20 at dawn. Can replace any roll (his or others) with portent die.

**Spell Mastery.** Can cast *detect magic* and *mage armor* at will without spell slots.

**Scholar of the Godsfall.** Expert on World-Splitter Components and ancient magic.

#### Actions

**Quarterstaff.** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target.  
*Hit:* 3 (1d6) bludgeoning damage, or 4 (1d8) if used with two hands.

**Ancient Artifact.** Carries World-Splitter Component #1 (see items). Can activate it as an action (devastating effects).

#### Spellcasting

**Spellcasting Ability:** Intelligence (spell save DC 18, +10 to hit)

**Cantrips (at will):** *fire bolt, mage hand, message, prestidigitation, shocking grasp*

**Spells Prepared:**
- 1st level (4 slots): *detect magic*, *mage armor*, *shield*, *identify*
- 2nd level (3 slots): *detect thoughts*, *misty step*, *see invisibility*
- 3rd level (3 slots): *counterspell*, *dispel magic*, *fly*
- 4th level (3 slots): *arcane eye*, *banishment*, *dimension door*
- 5th level (3 slots): *cone of cold*, *scrying*, *teleportation circle*
- 6th level (1 slot): *disintegrate*, *true seeing*
- 7th level (1 slot): *forcecage*, *teleport*
- 8th level (1 slot): *dominate monster*, *mind blank*
- 9th level (1 slot): *wish* (he plans to use this with Components)

#### Personality & Motivation

**Age:** 52  
**Appearance:** Scholar's robes, grey hair, intense eyes, surrounded by books and maps, focused, intelligent

**Personality:**
- Brilliant scholar and historian
- True believer in his cause
- Well-intentioned extremist
- Sees himself as humanity's savior
- Willing to sacrifice millions for "greater good"
- Not evilâ€”just convinced he's right

**Background:**
- Studied Godsfall history for 30 years
- Discovered World-Splitter Components exist
- Believes he can "remake" reality to eliminate war, poverty, suffering
- Gathered cult of followers (The Unbound)
- Sees both kingdoms as obstacles to better world
- Genuinely believes his plan will save humanity

**Motivation:**
- End suffering through restructuring reality
- Use World-Splitter Components to create "perfect" world
- Destroy old systems (monarchies AND democracies)
- Establish benevolent centralized control
- Sees himself as architect of utopia
- Blind to what he might destroy in the process

---

### **Corvus'S Pitch**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*He spreads a mapâ€”not of current Tirvandor, but of something else. Ancient. Before the Godsfall.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Both kingdoms are corrupt. Dawnblade serves a tyranny that oppresses millions. Valen serves a democracy that's descending into mob rule. They're not oppositesâ€”they're different flavors of failure.*
>
{{descriptive
*But there's a third option. During the Godsfall, when gods fought and shattered reality, they left something behind. Fragments of divine powerâ€”the World-Splitter Components.*
>
{{descriptive
*I've spent 30 years researching them. I've found one. Three more remain. With all five, I can use them to... restructure reality. End war. End poverty. End the suffering caused by flawed governments.*
>
{{descriptive
*Imagine a world without kings OR mobs. A world of true orderâ€”not Thaldros's oppressive order, but rational, benevolent coordination. Resources distributed fairly. Conflicts resolved peacefully. Everyone fed, housed, safe.*
>
{{descriptive
*That's what I'm building. Join me. Help me find the remaining Components. Help me save humanity from itself."*

**The "contract" he offers is more like a manifesto:**

**The Offer:**
- **Upfront Payment:** 1,000 gold pieces (least of three)
- **Per Mission:** 500-1,000gp + share of recovered artifacts
- **Authority:** None (you're outside the law)
- **Protection:** The Unbound network (underground cells)
- **Post-"War" Rewards:** Position as Wardens in New Order (govern regions)

**The Expectations:**
- Locate and retrieve World-Splitter Components
- Sabotage BOTH kingdoms (neither can win)
- Recruit powerful allies to the cause
- Publicly: "Fighting for freedom from both tyrannies"
- Privately: "Enabling reality restructuring"

---

### **Questions & Answers**

**If PCs ask questions:**

**"You're insane."**
{{descriptive
*"Am I? Look at history. Monarchies oppress. Democracies collapse. Theocracies control. Every system fails because humans are flawed. But what if we could... optimize? Remove the flaws? That's not insanityâ€”that's vision."*

**"What do these Components actually do?"**
{{descriptive
*"They were used by gods during the Godsfall to... alter fundamental reality. Think of reality as a tapestry. The Components allow you to reweave specific threads. With all five, coordinated properly, we can restructure society at a foundational level.*
>
{{descriptive
*No more warâ€”conflict becomes neurologically impossible. No more povertyâ€”resources redistribute automatically. No more tyrannyâ€”power structures optimize for collective good."*

**"That sounds like you're removing free will."**
{{descriptive
*(Pauses, considering)*
{{descriptive
*"That's... a philosophical question. Is 'free will' to starve, wage war, and oppress each other truly freedom? Or is it a luxury we can't afford? I'm offering freedom FROM suffering. That's real freedom."*

**"What if you're wrong?"**
{{descriptive
*"Then millions continue suffering under failed systems. At least I'm TRYING to fix it. Dawnblade maintains oppression. Valen enables chaos. I offer actual change. Which is most moral?"*

**Insight DC 16:**
- Corvus is absolutely sincere
- He's brilliant but potentially delusional
- He genuinely believes he's saving the world
- He's aware using Components might kill millions
- He considers it acceptable cost for "perfect" future
- He's charismatic cult leader who believes own rhetoric

**Persuasion DC 18 (to get him to reveal the cost):**
{{descriptive
*"You want to know the truth? Using all five Components will... disrupt reality temporarily. The restructuring process might kill... 10-20% of population. Maybe 30%.*
>
{{descriptive
*That's millions dead. I'm aware. I've done the calculations. I've spent three years agonizing over this decision.*
>
{{descriptive
*But if we DON'T act? Wars kill millions over decades. Poverty kills millions over centuries. I'm offering to save billions at the cost of millions. That's... that's utilitarian calculus.*
>
{{descriptive
*I don't LIKE it. But I'll do it. Because someone has to make hard choices."*

---

### **Corvus'S Secret Agenda**

**What he's NOT telling PCs:**

1. **The Cost:** Actually 30-40% fatality rate (he's minimizing)
2. **Free Will:** Components WILL remove free will in restructured reality
3. **Permanence:** Effect is permanentâ€”no going back
4. **His Instability:** Proximity to Component #1 is affecting his sanity
5. **The Unbound:** Some followers are extremists who want chaos, not utopia

**This information revealed later in Quest 2.3 (The Double Cross)**

---

## The Investigation Phase

**After meeting all three:**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*Three offers. Three visions. Three futures.*
>
{{descriptive
*Dawnblade offers gold and order through tyranny. Valen offers ideals and chaos through democracy. Corvus offers transformation through apocalypse.*
>
{{descriptive
*You have three days to decide. All three recruiters made that clearâ€”this opportunity won't wait forever. War is coming. Choose a side. Or try to play them all.*

---

### **Gathering Information**

**PCs can investigate all three factions before committing.**

**Suggested Activities:**

1. **Talk to NPCs from Act I**
   - Varak or Kael (guild leader): What do they think?
   - Mira (info broker): What rumors has she heard?
   - NPCs from previous quests: Which side did they choose?

2. **Research the Factions**
   - History checks about Thaldros
   - Investigation checks about Aethoria
   - Arcana checks about World-Splitter Components

3. **Observe Faction Actions**
   - Follow Dawnblade's soldiers
   - Watch Valen meet with contacts
   - Investigate Unbound hideout

---

### **Information Gathering Results**

**About Thaldros (History DC 15):**
- Kingdom has ruled 500+ years
- Stable but oppressive
- Efficient bureaucracy
- Common folk have little freedom but relative safety
- Recent decades: increasing corruption
- Marcus Blackwood case (if PCs know about it) is example of injustice

**About Aethoria (History DC 14):**
- Republic formed 80 years ago through revolution
- Democratic but unstable
- Mob rule common
- Amazing cultural output (art, science)
- Recent years: increasing corruption and faction fighting
- Many senators as corrupt as monarchs

**About the Unbound (Arcana DC 16):**
- Cult formed 10 years ago
- Led by Corvus Blackwood (scholar-turned-prophet)
- Obsessed with Godsfall artifacts
- Growing membership (2,000+ followers)
- Some members genuinely idealistic
- Others are apocalyptic extremists
- World-Splitter Components are REAL and DANGEROUS

---

### **Talking TO Act I Npcs**

**If PCs ask Varak (or Kael):**

**Varak (Iron Guild):**
{{descriptive
*"Thaldros. Always Thaldros. Order beats chaos every time. Aethoria's democracy is mob rule. And The Unbound? Cult nonsense. Take Dawnblade's gold and help maintain civilization."*

**Kael (Black Chains):**
{{descriptive
*"Play all three if you can. Get paid by everyone. When the war ends, whoever wins will need mercenaries. Loyalty is for soldiers. We're businessmen."*

**Mira (Info Broker):**
{{descriptive
*"Here's what I know: Dawnblade is honorable but following dishonorable orders. Valen is genuine but naive. Corvus is brilliant but insane. Pick your poison."*

**PCs from Quest 1.5 (if relevant):**

**If helped Marcus Blackwood:**
{{descriptive
*(Letter from Marcus, now in exile)*
{{descriptive
*"If you're reading this, war has begun. I urge you: side with Aethoria. Thaldros proved its injustice when it tried to silence me. Democracy is flawed, but it's our only hope against tyranny."*

**If delivered Marcus to trial:**
{{descriptive
*(Crown officials remember you favorably)*
{{descriptive
*"The crown appreciates your service. Commander Dawnblade has been instructed to offer you premium compensation."*

---

## The Choice

**After investigation, PCs must choose (or try to delay):**

### **Option 1: JOIN THALDROS**

**What You Get:**
- 2,500gp upfront (deposited immediately)
- Royal authority (legal backing)
- Political connections
- Highest pay per mission
- Post-war lands/titles

**What It Means:**
- Fighting for oppressive monarchy
- Some missions are war crimes
- You're tools of tyranny
- Common folk will hate you
- But you're on strongest side

**Immediate Effect:**
- Commander Dawnblade pleased
- Envoy Valen disappointed
- Corvus marks you as enemy
- Quest 2.2-T begins (Thaldros mission)

---

### **Option 2: JOIN AETHORIA**

**What You Get:**
- 1,500gp upfront (less than Thaldros)
- Popular support (common folk help)
- Moral high ground (fighting tyranny)
- Moderate pay per mission
- Post-war gratitude and recognition

**What It Means:**
- Fighting for unstable democracy
- Some missions require compromise
- You're revolutionaries
- Crown will hunt you
- But you're fighting for ideals

**Immediate Effect:**
- Envoy Valen grateful
- Commander Dawnblade disappointed but respectful
- Corvus sees potential allies
- Quest 2.2-A begins (Aethoria mission)

---

### **Option 3: Join The Unbound**

**What You Get:**
- 1,000gp upfront (least gold)
- Ancient artifacts access
- Underground network
- Low pay but artifact shares
- Post-"restructuring" positions as Wardens

**What It Means:**
- Fighting for apocalyptic cult
- Missions involve reality-warping artifacts
- You're terrorists to both kingdoms
- Everyone will hunt you
- But you're trying to "save" the world

**Immediate Effect:**
- Corvus thrilled
- Both Dawnblade AND Valen mark you as enemies
- Hunted by law
- Quest 2.2-U begins (Unbound mission)

---

### **Option 4: PLAY MULTIPLE SIDES (Double/Triple Agent)**

**Persuasion DC 16 with each faction to accept you while claiming loyalty**

**What You Get:**
- Multiple upfront payments (if successful)
- Access to all networks
- Maximum information
- Can switch sides as needed
- Highest potential profit

**What It Means:**
- Living a lie to everyone
- Constant Deception checks
- Will be discovered eventually (Quest 2.3)
- When exposed, ALL factions become enemies
- High risk, high reward

**Immediate Effect:**
- All factions think you're loyal
- You receive missions from multiple sources
- Must juggle commitments
- Consequences delayed until Quest 2.3

---

### **Option 5: REFUSE ALL**

**What You Get:**
- Independence
- Freedom to take contracts from anyone
- No faction commitments
- Can work for any as freelancer
- Maintain neutrality

**What It Means:**
- Lower pay (no upfront bonuses)
- No faction backing
- Fewer opportunities
- Must navigate war as independent
- Harder but freer path

**Immediate Effect:**
- All three recruiters disappointed
- Can still be hired on per-mission basis
- Quest 2.2 has different structure (freelance)

---

## Rewards

**Based on choice:**

**If THALDROS:** 2,500gp upfront  
**If AETHORIA:** 1,500gp upfront  
**If UNBOUND:** 1,000gp upfront  
**If MULTIPLE:** Variable (2,000-5,000gp if all deceived)  
**If REFUSE:** 0gp (but freedom)

**Plus:**
- Faction access
- First mission assignment
- Reputation with chosen side
- Enemies with other sides

---

## DM Guidance

### **Running the Three Meetings**

**Pacing:**
- Each meeting should take 30-45 minutes
- Let players ask questions
- Don't rush the decision
- This choice affects entire Act II

**Presenting Fairly:**
- Make all three appealing in different ways
- Don't telegraph "correct" choice
- All have valid arguments
- All have hidden flaws

**Player Agency:**
- Some players will choose quickly
- Some will agonize
- Both are valid
- Don't force a choice until they're ready

### **If Players Try to Delay**

**All three recruiters give 3-day deadline:**

{{descriptive
*"War waits for no one. Three days. Then we find other mercenaries."*

**After 3 days:**
- Offers expire (can still work freelance but no bonuses)
- Other mercenary groups are hired
- War begins without them

### **If Players Can't Agree**

**Party may split:**
- Some join Thaldros
- Some join Aethoria
- Some go independent
- This is VALID and creates interesting dynamics
- Campaign continues with divided party (harder but doable)

### **The "Right" Choice**

**There isn't one.**

- Thaldros offers stability through oppression
- Aethoria offers freedom through chaos
- Unbound offers transformation through apocalypse
- All are morally grey
- Let players decide what matters to them

---

## Transition to QUEST 2.2

**Based on choice, next quest is:**

- **Quest 2.2-T:** The Convoy (Thaldros mission)
- **Quest 2.2-A:** The Defector (Aethoria mission)
- **Quest 2.2-U:** The Component (Unbound mission)
- **Quest 2.2-M:** Mixed (if playing multiple sides)
- **Quest 2.2-F:** Freelance (if refused all)

**Quest 2.1 Complete**

3. **Corvus Blackwood** (Unbound Wizard/Prophet, CR 9)

All have complete stat blocks, personalities, motivations, and secrets.

# ðŸ”¥ Quest 2.2-U: The Component
## Unbound Mission

**Level:** 7 | **Duration:** 2-3 sessions

### **[Beginning section from previous response through The Component discovery]**

---

### **The Moral Choice**

**PCs must decide:**

#### **Option 1: DELIVER TO CORVUS (Complete Mission)**

**Actions:**
- Take Component back to Corvus
- Help his apocalyptic plan progress
- Enable "reshaping" of reality

**Consequences:**
- Full payment: 1,000gp + 1 ancient artifact
- Reputation: +5 with Unbound
- Component now in Corvus's hands (2 of 5 collected)
- Apocalypse one step closer
- You've enabled potential mass death

**Corvus's reaction:**
{{descriptive
*"Perfect! This is brilliant work. Two Components secured. Three remain. Together, we'll save the worldâ€”whether it wants to be saved or not."*

---

#### **Option 2: DESTROY COMPONENT**

**Actions:**
- Attempt to destroy the artifact
- Use magic, smashing, etc.

**Reality:**
- Component is nearly indestructible
- Requires *disintegrate* spell or similar high-level magic
- DC 18 Intelligence (Arcana) to figure out how

**If destroyed:**
- No payment (mission failed)
- Reputation: -10 with Unbound (hunted)
- Component eliminated (apocalypse harder to achieve)
- World slightly safer
- Corvus becomes enemy

**Corvus's reaction:**
{{descriptive
*"You DESTROYED it? Centuries of research! The hope of humanity! You've doomed millions to continued suffering. I'll never forgive this."*

---

#### **Option 3: KEEP COMPONENT**

**Actions:**
- Take artifact for yourself
- Don't return to Corvus
- Power in your hands (corrupting?)

**Consequences:**
- No payment (stole from employer)
- Reputation: -10 with Unbound (hunted)
- Component's influence on you (corruption)
- Both kingdoms hunt you (want Component)
- Future plot: What do YOU do with it?

**Every long rest: Wisdom save DC 14 or Component influences your decisions**

---

#### **Option 4: GIVE TO OPPOSING FACTION**

**Actions:**
- Deliver Component to Thaldros or Aethoria
- Betray Corvus
- Let kingdom study/use it

**Consequences:**
- Payment: 3,000gp from kingdom (major prize)
- Reputation: -10 with Unbound (hunted)
- Reputation: +10 with kingdom
- Kingdom now has Component (also dangerous)
- They'll study it for military advantage
- Different apocalypse risk

**Kingdom reaction:**
{{descriptive
*"Extraordinary! Our scholars will study this. Its power could win the war. You've served [kingdom name] well. You're a hero."*

**Later (Quest 2.4): Learn kingdom is weaponizing it**

---

#### **Option 5: HIDE COMPONENT**

**Deception DC 17:**

**Plan:**
- Claim Component was destroyed in trap
- Hide it somewhere secret
- Keep its location known only to you

**If successful:**
- Half payment: 500gp (failed mission)
- Component hidden (future plot point)
- Neither Corvus nor kingdoms have it
- World safer for now
- You know where ultimate power is buried

---

### **Aftermath**

**If Component delivered:**

**Two Weeks Later:**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*You hear rumors. The Unbound are becoming more active. More aggressive. Corvus is gathering followersâ€”hundreds joining. He's promising salvation. A better world. An end to war.*
>
{{descriptive
*But there's something in his eyes nowâ€”a fervor that wasn't there before. Proximity to two Components is affecting him. He's more convinced than ever that his path is right.*
>
{{descriptive
*You helped him get closer to that goal. For better or worse.*

---

**If Component destroyed/stolen:**

**Two Weeks Later:**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*The Unbound are furious. Corvus put a bounty on your headsâ€”2,000 gold, dead or alive. You're hunted by cultists who believe you destroyed their salvation.*
>
{{descriptive
*But othersâ€”scholars, clergy, common folkâ€”thank you quietly. "You may have saved us," one priest says. "Those Components are too dangerous for anyone."*
>
{{descriptive
*Whether you did right or wrong, you made a powerful enemy.*

---

## ðŸ“‹ Multiple Factions Option

**If PCs are working for multiple factions simultaneously:**

### **The Juggling Act**

**They receive multiple missions:**

**Thaldros wants:** Convoy destroyed  
**Aethoria wants:** Thorne extracted  
**Unbound wants:** Component retrieved

**PCs must:**
1. Complete all three (nearly impossible timing)
2. Prioritize one, fail others
3. Try creative solutions

**Example Creative Solution:**
- Complete Unbound mission first (3 days)
- Then split party: half does convoy, half does extraction
- High risk, high reward

**Consequences:**
- If succeed all: Maximum gold (5,000gp+)
- If fail any: That faction becomes suspicious
- Eventually discovered (Quest 2.3)
- All factions turn on you when revealed

---

## ðŸŽ¯ Quest COMPLETION

### **Experience & Rewards**

**Based on choices:**

**Quest 2.2-T (Convoy):**
- If completed: 2,000gp + Thaldros trust
- If refused: 0-500gp + Thaldros suspicion
- If exposed: Possible arrest

**Quest 2.2-A (Defector):**
- If delivered: 1,500gp + Aethoria trust
- If turned over: 0gp + moral clarity
- If public trial: 750gp + forced transparency

**Quest 2.2-U (Component):**
- If delivered: 1,000gp + artifact + Unbound trust
- If destroyed: 0gp + world safer
- If sold: 3,000gp + kingdom trust

**Level Up:**
- All PCs should reach **Level 8** after Quest 2.2
- New class features
- Increased spell power
- Ready for Act II escalation

---

## DM Guidance

### **Running Parallel Missions**

**Each mission tests different moral boundaries:**

**Thaldros (Convoy):**
- Tests: Willingness to harm innocents
- Theme: Collateral damage
- Question: "How far for gold?"

**Aethoria (Defector):**
- Tests: Justice vs pragmatism
- Theme: Moral compromise
- Question: "Does the end justify the means?"

**Unbound (Component):**
- Tests: Power vs safety
- Theme: Playing with fire
- Question: "Should some knowledge be forbidden?"

### **No Right Answers**

**All three missions are morally grey:**
- Completing helps your faction but has moral cost
- Refusing weakens faction but preserves conscience
- Creative solutions are possible but risky

**Don't judge players:**
- Present situation fairly
- Show consequences
- Let them decide
- All choices are valid

### **Consequences Matter**

**These choices echo through Act II:**

**If killed refugees (Convoy):**
- Civilian NPCs distrust you
- Aethoria sees you as monsters
- Thaldros gives more "difficult" missions

**If protected war criminal (Defector):**
- Justice subverted
- Survivors remember
- But Aethoria wins intelligence advantage

**If delivered Component:**
- Apocalypse closer
- Corvus more powerful
- World more dangerous

**Track all consequences for later quests**

---

## Transition to QUEST 2.3

**Regardless of mission outcome:**

After 1-2 weeks, **Quest 2.3: The Double Cross** begins.

**Setup:**
- Your faction has been lying to you
- Evidence emerges of betrayal
- Must decide how to respond

**Preview:**

**Read Aloud (End Of Session):**

{{descriptive
*You completed your first major mission. Gold in hand. Reputation building. Everything seems fine.*
>
{{descriptive
*Then, late one night, you receive an anonymous letter. No signature. Just evidenceâ€”documents, testimonies, proof.*
>
{{descriptive
*Your faction has been lying to you. About everything.*

**[Quest 2.3 will reveal the Double Cross]**

## New Items For Compendium

### **World-Splitter Component #2**
*Artifact (divine fragment), legendary*

*A crystalline shard glowing with impossible colors. Fragment of power that ended the Godsfall. Dangerous to touch. Catastrophic if misused.*

**Properties:**
- **Reality Sense:** Holder can sense distortions in reality within 1 mile
- **Divine Fragment:** Counts as holy symbol for all deities (living or dead)
- **Corrupting Influence:** Wisdom save DC 14 each long rest or become obsessed with its power
- **Indestructible:** Can only be destroyed by *disintegrate* or *wish*

**If Used (Do Not Do This):**
- Can cast *reality break* once (custom 9th level spell)
- Tears hole in reality, devastating 1-mile radius
- 10d10 force damage to all creatures (no save)
- Reality distorted permanently in area
- User must succeed DC 18 Con save or die

**Campaign Role:**
- Central to Unbound plot
- Corvus needs 5 to "reshape" reality
- Both kingdoms want them
- Incredibly dangerous

**Acquisition:**
- Quest 2.2-U (if retrieve from Old Kaer vault)

---

### **Ancient Vault Artifacts**

**Found in Old Kaer vault (if searched):**

1. **Ring of Mind Shielding** (Uncommon)
2. **Cloak of Protection** (Uncommon)
3. **Wand of Web** (Uncommon, 7 charges)
4. **Dusty spellbooks** (3d4 wizard spells, random)

**PCs can take 1-2 items depending on time and carrying capacity**

# Quest 2.3: The Double Cross

## Blood & Coin Campaign - Act II

**Level:** 8  
**Duration:** 3-4 sessions  
**Objective:** Discover your faction is betraying youâ€”survive and decide response  
**Key NPCs:** Varies by faction  
**Rewards:** Survival (gold secondary)  
**Theme:** "Trust no one"

---

## Quest Setup

**Time:** Two weeks after Quest 2.2

**What's Happened:**
- You completed 2-3 missions for your chosen faction
- Built reputation and trust
- Earned significant gold
- Everything seems fine

**Then the truth emerges.**

---

## The Revelation

**Session begins normally. Then:**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*You're returning to your lodgings after another successful mission. Gold in hand, reputation solid. You're becoming important players in this war.*
>
{{descriptive
*Then you find it: an envelope slipped under your door. No seal. No signature. Just a note:*
>
{{descriptive
*"They're lying to you. They've been lying from the start. Meet me at the Old Mill, midnight. Come alone. I have proof. â€”A Friend"*
>
{{descriptive
*Attached: a single document. It looks official. And damning.*

**The document varies by faction...**

---

# ðŸ° IF Working For Thaldros

## The Document

**Royal Military Memo (appears authentic):**

{{descriptive
**FROM:** Royal Command  
{{descriptive
**TO:** Commander Dawnblade  
{{descriptive
**RE:** Mercenary Operationsâ€”Asset Disposal  
> 
{{descriptive
*Approved contractors [your group name] have performed adequately. Continue utilizing for sensitive operations through war's end.*
>
{{descriptive
*Post-conflict: Initiate Protocol Scapegoat. Frame contractors for documented atrocities (Thornwood Convoy, civilian casualties, etc.). Public trial. Execution.*
>
{{descriptive
*Rationale: Crown maintains clean image. Mercenaries bear responsibility for necessary wartime actions. Loose ends eliminated.*
>
{{descriptive
*Authorization: King's Seal*

**Investigation DC 14:** Document appears genuine (royal watermarks, proper formatting, real signatures)

---

## The Meeting

**Old Mill, Midnight**

**If PCs attend:**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*The Old Mill is abandoned, dark, perfect for clandestine meetings. You arrive carefully, weapons ready.*
>
{{descriptive
*A figure emerges from shadowsâ€”cloaked, face hidden. Female voice, low and urgent:*
>
{{descriptive
*"You came. Good. You're smarter than most." She tosses you a leather folder. "More proof. Orders. Correspondence. They're planning to execute you. Make you martyrs. Pin everything on 'rogue mercenaries' while the crown stays pure."*

**The folder contains:**
- 12 more documents (authentic)
- Execution orders pre-signed
- Lists of "mercenary crimes" to publicize
- Timeline: arrest you 3 days after war ends
- Commander Dawnblade's signature on several

---

## Npc: The Informant (Captain Sarah Vale)

*Medium humanoid (human), neutral good*

**Appearance:** 30s, royal military uniform under cloak, blonde hair, haunted eyes, guilty expression

**Who She Is:**
- Captain in Thaldros military
- Works under Dawnblade
- Has conscience (unlike most)
- Disgusted by Scapegoat Protocol
- Risking execution to warn you

**Armor Class:** 16 (breastplate)  
**Hit Points:** 58 (9d8 + 18)  
**Speed:** 30 ft.

**STR** 15 (+2) | **DEX** 14 (+2) | **CON** 14 (+2)  
**INT** 12 (+1) | **WIS** 13 (+1) | **CHA** 14 (+2)

**Saving Throws:** Str +5, Con +5  
**Skills:** Athletics +5, Insight +4, Perception +4, Persuasion +5  
**Senses:** Passive Perception 14  
**Languages:** Common  
**Challenge:** 3 (700 XP)

**Combat Veteran.** Advantage on saves vs fear.

**Second Wind (Recharge 5-6).** Heal 1d10 + 9 as bonus action.

#### Actions

**Multiattack.** Two longsword attacks.

**Longsword.** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target.  
*Hit:* 6 (1d8 + 2) slashing damage.

**Heavy Crossbow.** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, range 100/400 ft., one target.  
*Hit:* 7 (1d10 + 2) piercing damage.

#### Personality

**Motivation:**
- Can't stomach executing honorable mercenaries
- Seen too much corruption in crown
- This was final straw
- Willing to defect if you'll have her

**What She Knows:**
- Scapegoat Protocol is real
- Dawnblade is conflicted but will follow orders
- Crown has done this before (you're not first)
- War's end is 2-3 months away (timeline urgent)

**What She Wants:**
- Warn you
- Maybe defect with you
- Prevent injustice
- Doesn't expect to survive this

---

### **Confrontation With Dawnblade**

**If PCs confront her with evidence:**

**Read Aloud:**

{{descriptive
*You storm into Dawnblade's office, documents in hand. She looks up, sees what you're holding, and her face falls.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Ah." She stands slowly. "Sarah. I should have watched her more closely."*
>
{{descriptive
*She doesn't deny it. Doesn't even try.*
>
{{descriptive
*"Yes. It's real. Scapegoat Protocol. Orders from high command. When the war ends, you'll be arrested. Tried for war crimes. Executed. The crown needs someone to blame, and mercenaries are perfect."*

**Insight DC 12:** She's deeply uncomfortable but resigned to following orders

**If PCs get angry:**

{{descriptive
*"You think I LIKE this? I'm a soldier. I follow orders. Even orders I hate. That's the oath I took. That's the burden I bear."*
>
{{descriptive
*(Her voice cracks slightly)*
>
{{descriptive
*"For what it's worth... you're good people. You did the dirty work no one else would do. And yes, you'll die for it. That's the price of serving power. I'm sorry."*

**If PCs threaten her:**

{{descriptive
*"Kill me if you want. Won't change anything. Scapegoat Protocol is official. My replacement will execute it. You can't fight the entire kingdom."*

---

### **The CHOICE (Thaldros Path)**

**PCs must decide:**

#### **Option 1: FLEE THALDROS**

**Actions:**
- Abandon faction immediately
- Become fugitives
- Find new employer or go independent

**Consequences:**
- Wanted by entire Thaldros military
- Bounty: 5,000gp (dead or alive)
- Lose all Thaldros connections
- Can't return to kingdom-controlled areas
- Sarah defects with you (if you let her)
- Survive but hunted

---

#### **Option 2: SWITCH TO AETHORIA**

**Actions:**
- Contact Envoy Valen
- Offer to defect with intelligence
- Join Aethoria cause

**Envoy Valen's Response:**
{{descriptive
*"Thaldros betrayed you? I'm not surprised. They devour their own. Join us. We'll protect you. Plus, your intelligence on Thaldros operations is invaluable. Welcome to the Republic."*

**Consequences:**
- Aethoria pays 2,000gp for defection + intelligence
- Reputation: +10 with Aethoria
- Reputation: -20 with Thaldros (traitors)
- Now working for opposite side
- War continues, you've switched teams

---

#### **Option 3: BLACKMAIL THALDROS**

**Intimidation DC 18 to make Dawnblade back down:**

**If successful:**
{{descriptive
*"You want to negotiate? Fine. I'll report Scapegoat Protocol 'failed' due to security leak. You'll be marked as liabilities instead of assets. They won't actively hunt you, but they won't protect you either. You'll be on your own. Deal?"*

**Consequences:**
- Thaldros backs off (you're too risky to arrest)
- No payment, no support, no protection
- Technically independent
- Can work for anyone now
- Thaldros watches you but doesn't attack
- Uneasy truce

---

#### **Option 4: ACCEPT FATE**

**Decide to stay loyal despite betrayal:**

**Why PCs might choose this:**
- Believe in Thaldros cause despite corruption
- Pragmatic acceptance of mercenary risks
- Too invested to quit
- Think they can survive trial somehow

**Consequences:**
- Continue working for Thaldros
- Know you'll be arrested when war ends
- Try to gather evidence to exonerate selves
- Or plan escape for later
- Living on borrowed time

---

#### **Option 5: GO ROGUE**

**Kill Dawnblade, expose Scapegoat Protocol publicly:**

**If you kill her:**
- Immediate alarm
- 20 **Thaldros Guards** respond (CR 1/8 each)
- Must fight way out or die

**If you expose protocol:**
- Publish documents to press/public
- Major scandal for crown
- Some nobles support you, others hunt you
- Public opinion divided
- Crown furious but can't openly retaliate

**Consequences:**
- Massive political fallout
- Thaldros government embarrassed
- You're heroes to some, traitors to others
- Can't work in Thaldros territory
- Crown sends assassins privately

---

**TO:** Envoy Valen

>

>

>
{{descriptive
*(He stops, hearing himself)*
>
{{descriptive

**Insight DC 13:** Valen is genuinely conflictedâ€”he really believes in democracy but has rationalized compromise

**If PCs press him:**

>

*(Ashamed)*

### **The CHOICE (Aethoria Path)**

**PCs must decide:**

#### **Option 1: FLEE AETHORIA**

**Actions:**
- Leave Republic immediately
- Become independent
- Avoid both kingdoms

**Consequences:**
- Wanted by Aethoria government
- Bounty: 3,000gp
- Lost faith in democracy (it failed)
- Can work as independents
- Cynical but free

---

#### **Option 2: SWITCH TO THALDROS**

**Actions:**
- Contact Commander Dawnblade
- Offer intelligence on Aethoria
- Join monarchy

**Dawnblade's Response:**
{{descriptive
*"Aethoria betrayed you? Democracy always fails. Welcome to the side of order. We'll pay well for your intelligence. 3,000 gold. Plus, when we win, you'll be rewarded properly."*

**Consequences:**
- Thaldros pays 3,000gp for defection
- Reputation: +10 with Thaldros
- Reputation: -20 with Aethoria (traitors)
- Irony: fought for freedom, joined tyranny
- But at least tyranny is honest about being tyranny

---

#### **Option 3: SAVE DEMOCRACY**

**Work with Valen to expose corrupt senators:**

**Persuasion DC 16 to convince Valen to help:**

**If successful:**
{{descriptive
*"You're right. If democracy is worth fighting for, it's worth fighting for HONESTLY. Help me. We'll expose the corrupt senators. Force public trials. Restore true democracy. It's riskyâ€”they'll try to kill usâ€”but it's RIGHT."*

**The Campaign:**
- Gather more evidence (3 skill challenges)
- Build coalition of honest senators (social encounters)
- Public reveal at senate session (dramatic scene)
- Face political assassination attempts (2 combat encounters)

**If successful:**
- Corrupt senators removed
- Democracy preserved
- You're heroes of the TRUE revolution
- Aethoria remains flawed but honest
- Rare good ending for this path

**Consequences:**
- Partial payment: 1,000gp (from grateful honest senators)
- Reputation: +15 with common people
- Reputation: +5 with honest senators
- Reputation: -20 with corrupt politicians (now enemies)
- Democracy survives but wounded

---

#### **Option 4: ACCEPT OLIGARCHY**

**Decide corrupt senate is better than Thaldros:**

**Rationalization:**
- "Guided democracy" is still better than monarchy
- Pragmatic acceptance
- Lesser evil
- At least they'll rule competently

**Consequences:**
- Continue working for Aethoria
- Know democracy is dying
- Help establish oligarchy
- Payment continues but conscience damaged
- Become tools of hypocrisy

---

#### **Option 5: ANARCHIST REVOLUTION**

**Burn it all downâ€”expose both kingdoms:**

**Actions:**
- Leak corruption evidence publicly
- Reveal Thaldros Scapegoat Protocol too
- Undermine both governments
- Create power vacuum

**Consequences:**
- Both kingdoms destabilized
- Chaos spreads
- You're wanted by EVERYONE
- Common folk divided (some support, some blame you)
- Unbound (Corvus) sees opportunity
- You've started regional collapse

## The Meeting
